Limited Mulazamah for a Traveller Defendant
Explaining limited mulazamah for a traveller defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mulazamah for a traveller defendant and explain the reasoning based on preventing hardship.

Core Idea
A traveller defendant is only required to be accompanied for the court session to avoid unjust harm to his travel.

In this passage, we examine how the Hanafi school balances the plaintiff's right to secure the defendant with the defendant's right to travel. The text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that when the defendant is a traveller (gharib), the mulazamah is limited to the duration of the court session. This ruling is grounded in the principle of avoiding harm (la darar), ensuring that litigation does not become a hardship for the traveller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defendant's status
Determine if the defendant is a traveller (gharib) away from his hometown. This triggers the special ruling.
The term 'gharib' is defined as a traveller (musafir).
2
Determine the limit of mulazamah
The plaintiff may only accompany the defendant for the duration of a single court session (majlis al-qadi). No longer.
Similarly, a surety (kafil) is only required until the end of the session.
3
Understand the reasoning
The ruling is based on the need to avoid harm (darar) to the traveller by preventing his travel. Requiring more would cause undue hardship.
The reasoning is cited from al-Hidayah.
4
Note the scope of 'court session'
The session includes any sitting, even if the judge sits only once every fifteen days. The limit is not a fixed time but the session itself.
Referenced from al-Bazaziyyah.
5
Define 'gharib' as traveller
Confirm that 'gharib' means a person who is a traveller (musafir) and known to be so.
If the defendant is known to be a traveller, no surety is taken beyond the session.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو كان غريباً لازمه مقدار مجلس القاضي) وكذا لا يكفل إلا إلى آخر المجلس، فلو قال إلا أن يكون غريباً فإلى انتهاء مجلس القضاء لكان أولى. ليرجع إلى الملازمة والتكفيل وعلله في الهداية بأن في أخذ الكفيل والملازمة زيادة على ذلك إضراراً به بمنعه عن السفر ولا ضرر في هذا المقدار ظاهراً أطلق في مقدار مجلس القاضي فشمل ما إذا كان يجلس في كل خمسة عشر يوماً مرة ؛ كذا في البزازية. والمراد بالغريب المسافر لما في البزازية : لو كان المدعى عليه مسافراً وعرف ذلك منه لا يؤخذ منه كفيل وأجله
His statement: (And if he is a stranger, he accompanies him to the extent of the court session). Similarly, he does not give a surety except to the end of the session. So if he said 'unless he is a stranger, then until the end of the court session' it would be better. It returns to mulazamah and takfil, and its reasoning in al-Hidayah is that taking a surety and mulazamah beyond that would cause harm by preventing him from travelling, and there is no apparent harm in this amount. He [the author] spoke generally regarding the extent of the court session, so it includes the case where he sits once every fifteen days; likewise in al-Bazaziyyah. And what is meant by 'gharib' is the traveller, as in al-Bazaziyyah: If the defendant is a traveller and that is known of him, no surety is taken from him, and its term...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage addresses the special treatment of a traveller (gharib) defendant. The matn states that if the defendant is a traveller, the plaintiff's right to mulazamah is limited to the duration of the court session (majlis al-qadi). Similarly, the defendant need only provide a surety for the same period. The reasoning, based on al-Hidayah, is that requiring a surety or mulazamah beyond the session would unduly harm the traveller by preventing his journey. The limit is the court session, even if the judge sits only once every fifteen days. The term 'gharib' is defined as a traveller (musafir), as specified in al-Bazaziyyah, and if the defendant is known to be a traveller, no surety is taken from him at all beyond the session.

Key Terms
غريب (gharīb): A traveller (musafir) who is away from his hometown; applies to the defendant in litigation.
مجلس القاضي (majlis al-qāḍī): The sitting of the judge in court; the duration for which mulazamah is limited for a traveller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How long may a plaintiff accompany a traveller defendant according to the Hanafi school?
A) For three days
B) For the duration of the court session
C) For the entire duration of the journey
D) Until the end of the month

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school protects a traveller defendant by limiting mulazamah to the court session, balancing the plaintiff's right with the necessity of travel.

Mulazamah: The Claimant's Right to Follow the Defendant
Explains the ruling of mulazamah when the defendant refuses to provide a surety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mulazamah, identify its limits (mosque, no confinement), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on appointing a follower.

Core Idea
Mulazamah allows following the debtor, not imprisoning — and never in the mosque.

When a defendant refuses to provide a surety, the claimant has a right to secure his claim. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the tool of mulazamah: following the defendant wherever he goes, rather than confining him. It also reveals a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on whether the claimant can delegate this task to another person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
When the defendant refuses a surety, the claimant may follow him literally around with the debtor wherever he goes.
The ruling is stated in the matn: 'If he refuses, follow him.'
2
Understand the definition
Mulazamah is defined as going around with the defendant, not confining him to one place. The claimant goes where the debtor goes, but does not imprison him.
The commentary emphasizes: 'he does not require him to stay in a specific place.'
3
Note the mosque exception
The claimant cannot follow the defendant into a mosque, because the mosque is built for worship and such pursuit would violate its sanctity. This is the relied-upon position (wa bihi yufta).
The text cites al-Sughra: 'the madhhab with us is that he does not follow him in the mosque.'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa held that if the claimant appoints someone else to follow the debtor, the debtor may refuse. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that the debtor cannot refuse; the claimant may appoint an agent.
The ikhtilaf is based on the principle of agency without the opponent's consent.
5
Apply special cases
If the defendant is a woman, the claimant must hire a woman to follow her. If the defendant is a traveler, mulazamah is limited to the duration of the court session, to avoid preventing travel.
These exceptions are derived from the fatwa collections cited in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن أبى لازمه أي دار معه حيث دار أي بمقدار مدة التكفيل المذكورة. أشار إلى تفسير الملازمة بالدوران إلى أنه لا يلزمه في مكان معين. وفي الصغرى : المذهب عندنا أنه لا يلازمه في المسجد لأن المسجد بني لذكر الله تعالى وبه يفتى ثم قال فيها : وتفسير الملازمة أن يدور معه حيثما دار ويبعت معه أميناً حتى يدور معه. ورأيت في زيادات بعض المشايخ أن الطالب لو أمر غيره بملازمة مديونه فللمديون أن لا يرضى عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، وجعله فرعاً لمسألة التوكيل بغير رضا الخصم لكنه لا يحبسه في موضع لأن ذلك حبس وهو غير مستحق عليه بنفسه الدعوى ولا يشغله عن التصرف بل هو يتصرف والمدعي يدور معه، وإذا انتهى المطلوب إلى داره فإن الطالب لا يمنعه من الدخول إلى أهله بل يدخل المطلوب إلى أهله والملازم بجلس على باب داره؛ هكذا ذكر هنا وفي الزيادات أن المطلوب إذا أراد أن يدخل بيته فإما أن يأذن للمدعي في الدخول أو يجلس معه على باب الدار لأنه لو تركه حتى يدخل الدار وحده فربما يهرب من جانب آخر فيفوت ما هو المقصود منها. وفي تعليق أستاذنا : لو كان المدعى عليه امرأة فإن الطالب لا يلازمها بنفسه بل يستأجر امرأة فتلازمها . وفي أول كراهية الواقعات رجل له على امرأة حق فله أن يلازمها ويجلس معها ويقبض على ثيابها لأن هذا ليس بحرام فإن هربت ودخلت خربة فلا بأس بذلك إذا كان الرجل يأمن على نفسه ويكون بعيداً منها يحفظها بعينه لأن في هذه الخلوة ضرورة ا هـ. وأشار بملازمته إلى ملازمة المدعى لما في خزانة المفتين : إذا كان المدعى عليه متلافاً وأبى إعطاء الكفيل بالمدعي فللمدعي أن يلازم ذلك الشيء إلى أن يعطيه كفيلاً، وإن كان المدعي ضعيفاً. عن ذلك يضع الشيء على يد عدل ا هـ . وظاهر ما في السراج الوهاج أنه لا يلازمه إلا بإذن القاضي وذكر فيه أن منها أن يسكن حيث سكن. وفي المصباح : دار حول البيت يدور دوراً ودورانا طاف به ودوران الفلك تواتر حركاته بعضها إثر بعض من غير ثبوت ولا استقرار ومنه قولهم دارت المسألة أي كلما تعلقت بمحل توقف ثبوت الحكم على غيره فتنتقل إليه ثم بتوقف على الأول وهكذا ا قوله: (ولو) كان غريباً لازمه مقدار مجلس القاضي) وكذا لا يكفل إلا إلى آخر المجلس، فلو قال إلا أن يكون غريباً فإلى انتهاء مجلس القضاء لكان أولى. ليرجع إلى الملازمة والتكفيل وعلله في الهداية بأن في أخذ الكفيل والملازمة زيادة على ذلك إضراراً به بمنعه عن السفر ولا ضرر في هذا المقدار ظاهراً أطلق في مقدار مجلس القاضي فشمل ما إذا كان يجلس في كل خمسة عشر يوماً مرة ؛ كذا في البزازية. والمراد بالغريب المسافر لما في البزازية : لو كان المدعى عليه مسافراً وعرف ذلك منه لا يؤخذ منه كفيل وأجله إلى آخر المجلس، فإن برهن في المجلس وإلا خلى سبيله، ولو قال أنا أخرج غداً أو إلى ثلاثة أيام يكفله إلى وقت الخروج وإن أنكر الطالب خروجه نظر إلى زيه أو بعث من يثق به إلى رفقائه، فإن قالوا أعد للخروج معنا يكفله إلى وقت الخروج اهـ.
His saying: (If he refuses, follow him) i.e., go around with him wherever he goes, i.e., to the extent of the mentioned period of suretyship. He indicated the interpretation of mulazamah as moving around, meaning he does not require him to stay in a specific place. In al-Sughra: The madhhab with us is that he does not follow him in the mosque because the mosque is built for the remembrance of Allah, and with it is given fatwa. Then he said in it: The interpretation of mulazamah is that he goes around with him wherever he goes, and he sends a trustee with him to go around with him. I saw in the Ziyadat of some mashayikh that if the claimant orders someone else to follow his debtor, the debtor may not be pleased with that according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). He made it a branch of the issue of agency without the opponent's consent, but he does not imprison him in a place because that is imprisonment, which he is not entitled to by the mere claim, and it does not occupy him from his activities; rather he acts and the claimant goes around with him. When the defendant reaches his house, the claimant does not prevent him from entering upon his family; rather the defendant enters his family and the follower sits at the door of his house. Thus it is mentioned here and in al-Ziyadat that when the defendant wants to enter his house, either he permits the claimant to enter or he sits with him at the door of the house, because if he leaves him to enter the house alone, perhaps he might escape from another side, thus losing what was intended. In the commentary of our teacher: If the defendant is a woman, the claimant does not follow her himself but hires a woman to follow her. In the beginning of Karahiyya al-Waqi'at: A man who has a right against a woman may follow her, sit with her, and hold her clothes because this is not haram; if she flees and enters a ruin, there is no harm if the man is safe for himself and is distant from her, guarding her with his eye because in this seclusion there is necessity. (End) He indicated by his following the claimant's following, as in Khizanat al-Muftin: If the defendant is wasteful and refuses to give a surety to the claimant, the claimant may follow that thing until he gives him a surety; if the claimant is weak, he places the thing with a trustworthy person. (End) The apparent from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is that he does not follow him except with the permission of the judge, and he mentioned that among them is that he resides where he resides. In al-Misbah: He went around the house, turning around; it is said 'the issue circulated' meaning whenever it is attached to a place, the establishment of the ruling depends on another, so it transfers to it, then depends on the first, etc. His saying: (And if he is a stranger, he follows him for the duration of the judge's session) and likewise he is not given a surety except until the end of the session. If he said 'unless he is a stranger, then until the end of the court session', it would be better. This refers to mulazamah and suretyship, and he gave the reason in al-Hidayah that taking a surety and mulazamah beyond that is harmful by preventing him from travel, and there is no harm in this amount apparently. He made it absolute in the amount of the judge's session, so it includes if he sits once every fifteen days; as in al-Bazzaziyya. What is meant by 'stranger' is the traveler, as in al-Bazzaziyya: If the defendant is a traveler and that is known from him, he is not taken a surety from him, and his term is until the end of the session. If he proves (his claim) in the session, otherwise he is released. If he says 'I will leave tomorrow or in three days', he is given a surety until the time of departure. If the claimant denies his departure, he looks at his dress or sends someone he trusts to his companions; if they say 'he is ready to leave with us', he is given a surety until the time of departure. (End)
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling of mulazamah (following the debtor). The matn states: 'If he refuses, follow him.' The commentary explains that this means the claimant may go around with the defendant wherever he goes, but only for the duration of the suretyship period. Importantly, the claimant cannot confine the defendant to a specific place; he must follow him. The defendant cannot be followed into the mosque because the mosque is built for worship, and fatwa is given accordingly. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, if the claimant appoints someone else to follow the debtor, the debtor may refuse; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the debtor cannot refuse. The commentary also addresses cases where the defendant is a woman—the claimant must hire a woman to follow her. For a traveler defendant, the mulazamah is limited to the duration of the court session, and no surety is taken beyond that. The reasoning is that taking a surety or following beyond the session would harm the traveler by preventing his journey. The passage collects multiple authoritative sources (al-Sughra, al-Ziyadat, al-Hidayah, al-Bazzaziyya, etc.) to fully flesh out the ruling.

Key Terms
ملازمة (mulāzamah): Following the defendant wherever he goes as a means to secure payment or a surety, without confining him to one place.
كفيل (kafīl): A surety or guarantor for the defendant's appearance or payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, where may the claimant NOT follow the defendant who refuses a surety?
A) In the marketplace
B) In the mosque
C) At the defendant's house
D) In the judge's courtroom

Key Takeaway
Mulazamah is following, not imprisonment, and the mosque is protected from such pursuit.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

The Oath in Court: Swearing by Allah Only
States the ruling that the oath must be by Allah alone and discusses exceptions and disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that oaths in court must be by Allah alone, identify the hadith proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on swearing by divorce and manumission.

Core Idea
Only an oath by Allah is valid in court; swearing by divorce or manumission is haram and yields no legal effect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq al-Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq sets out the foundational principle for oaths in judicial proceedings. The matn declares that the oath must be by Allah, not by divorce or manumission, unless the opponent insists. The commentary provides the hadith proof and then delves into a significant intra-madhhab dispute about whether later judges may administer oaths by divorce due to society's diminished reverence for Allah's name. The discussion also addresses whether swearing by al-Rahman and al-Rahim counts as an oath, revealing a correction by later commentators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
State the rule: the oath must be by Allah. The exception: if the opponent insists, there is a minority view allowing swearing by divorce.
2
Locate the Dalil
The hadith: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' (Tirmidhi)
This hadith is the primary textual evidence.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The imperative 'فيحلف' (let him swear) indicates obligation, and the alternative 'أو ليذر' (or be silent) implies that only swearing by Allah is valid.
The imperative implies command; the alternative of silence excludes all other forms.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The majority (zahir al-riwaya) prohibit swearing by divorce/manumission. Some later scholars allow it if the opponent insists, but the fatwa is on prohibition.
The disagreement is about practical application in later times, not about the basic principle.
5
Evaluate the Sub-Issue of al-Rahman/al-Rahim
Some earlier texts claimed these names are not valid, but al-Maqdisi refuted this, confirming that all names of Allah are valid for oaths.
This shows that the definition of 'by Allah' includes all His names.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واليمين بالله تعالى لا بطلاق وعتاق إلا إذا ألح الخصم) لقوله عليه السلام «من كان حالفاً منكم فيحلف بالله أو ليذر (۱) . وفي خزانة المفتين واليمين بالله تعالى ذكر اسمه تعالى وهو أن يقول والله ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لا تحليف بغير هذا الاسم، فلو حلفه بالرحمن أو لا يكون يميناً ولم أره صريحاً فلا يحلف بغيره من طلاق وعتاق، وقيل في زماننا إذا ألح الخصم ساغ للقاضي أن يحلف بذلك لقلة المبالاة باليمين بالله تعالى؛ كذا في الهداية. وظاهره أنه خارج عن ظاهر الرواية فما كان ينبغي للمؤلف ذكره في المتن لأنه موضوع لظاهر أنه ضعيف أيضاً لما في الخلاصة والتحليف بالطلاق والعتاق والأيمان المغلظة لم يجوزه أكثر مشايخنا ا هـ . وفي الخانية : وإن أراد المدعي تحليفه بالطلاق والعتاق في ظاهر الرواية لا يجيبه القاضي إلى ذلك لأن التحليف بالطلاق والعتاق حرام، ومنهم من جوزه في زماننا والصحيح ما في ظاهر الرواية ا . وفي كتاب الحظر والإباحة من التتارخانية : والفتوى على عدم التحليف بالطلاق والعتاق ا هـ . وفي منية المفتي : لم يجزه أكثر مشايخنا وإن مست إليه الضرورة يفتى أن الرأي فيه للقاضي اتباعاً للبعض ا هـ . وفي خزانة المفتين كما في منية المفتي وزاد فلو حلفه القاضي بالطلاق فنكل وقضى بالمال لا ينفذ قضاؤه على قول الأكثر ا هـ. وظاهره أنه مفرع على قول الأكثر من أنه لا تحليف بهما فلا اعتبار بنكوله عنهما، وأما من قال بالتحليف بهما فيعتبر نكوله ويقضى به لأن التحليف بهما لرجاء النكول قوله : (فلو) حلفه بالرحمن أو الرحيم لا يكون يميناً ولم أره) رده العلامة المقدسي على ما نقل عنه الحموي بأنه قصور لوجود النص على خلافه فقد ذكروا في كتاب الأيمان أنه لو قال والرحمن أو الرحيم أو القادر فكل ذلك يمين ويدل عليه قولهم فيما إذا غلظ بذكر الصفة يحترز عن الإتيان بالواو لئلا تنكر اليمين، ونصوا هنا في تحليف الأخرس أن يقال له عهد الله عليك، ولا فرق بينه وبين الصحيح بل صرح بهذا في الصحيح، وصحح في روضة القضاة بأن الرحمن الرحيم وسائر أسماء الله تعالى تكون يميناً .اهـ. كذا في حاشية أبي السعود قوله : (نكوله) والظاهر من كلام الزيلعي خلافه حيث قال : وقال بعضهم يسوغ للقاضي أن يحلفه بهما إذا ألح الخصم لكن إذا نكل لا يقضى عليه بالنكول ولو قضى عليه بالنكول لا ينفذ اهـ. وفي غرر الأفكار مثله وعلله بقوله لامتناعه عما فليتأمل في هذا التعليل. وفي حاشية أبي السعود وفي الدر عن مصنف التنوير أنه هو منهي عنه (۱) رواه الترمذي في كتاب النذور باب . أحمد في مسنده (٢/ ٧).
His saying: (And the oath is by Allah, not by divorce or manumission, except if the opponent insists) because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' In Khizanat al-Muftin: The oath by Allah is the mention of His name, which is to say 'By Allah'. (End) Its apparent meaning is that there is no swearing by other than this name. So if he makes him swear by al-Rahman, it is not an oath, and I have not seen it explicitly. Therefore, he should not swear by other than it from divorce and manumission. It was said in our time: if the opponent insists, it is permissible for the judge to make him swear by that because of lack of concern for the oath by Allah; as in al-Hidayah. Its apparent meaning is that it is outside the zahir al-riwaya, so it was not proper for the author to mention it in the matn, because it is based on something that is also weak, as in al-Khulasa: 'Swearing by divorce, manumission, and severe oaths was not permitted by most of our mashayikh.' (End) In al-Khaniyya: If the claimant wants to make him swear by divorce and manumission, in zahir al-riwaya the judge does not respond to that, because swearing by divorce and manumission is haram. Some permitted it in our time, but the correct is what is in zahir al-riwaya. (End) In Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha from al-Tatarkhaniyya: The fatwa is on not swearing by divorce and manumission. (End) In Munyat al-Mufti: Most of our mashayikh did not permit it, even if necessity arises; it is opined that the judge has discretion following some. (End) In Khizanat al-Muftin as in Munyat al-Mufti, with addition: If the judge makes him swear by divorce and he refuses (nukul), and he judges against him for the property, his judgment is not executed according to the majority. (End) Its apparent meaning is that it is based on the majority saying that there is no swearing by them, so his nukul is not considered. As for those who said that swearing by them is allowed, his nukul is considered and judgment is given accordingly, because swearing by them is for hope of nukul. His saying: (If he makes him swear by al-Rahman or al-Rahim, it is not an oath, and I have not seen it explicitly) was refuted by al-Maqdisi, as reported from him by al-Hamawi, as being deficient because there is a text to the contrary. They mentioned in Kitab al-Ayman that if one says 'by al-Rahman' or 'by al-Rahim' or 'by al-Qadir', all of that is an oath. This is supported by their statement regarding when the oath is made severe by mentioning the attribute, to avoid using the waw so that the oath is not denied. And they explicitly stated here regarding the oath of the mute: 'the covenant of Allah is upon you' is said to him, and there is no difference between him and the healthy; rather this is explicitly stated in the sahih. And it was corrected in Rawdat al-Qudah that al-Rahman, al-Rahim, and all names of Allah are oaths. (End) This is as in Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud. His saying: (His nukul) The apparent from the speech of al-Zayla'i is the opposite: he said: Some said it is permissible for the judge to make him swear by them if the opponent insists, but if he refuses (nukul), no judgment is made against him for the nukul, and if he judges against him for the nukul, it is not executed. (End) In Ghurar al-Afkar, the same, and he gave the reason: because he refrained from that. So one should ponder this explanation. In Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud and in al-Durr from the author of al-Tanwir: it is something prohibited. (1) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Nudhur, chapter. Ahmad in his Musnad (2/7).
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on the oath in court. The matn states: 'The oath is by Allah, not by divorce or manumission, except if the opponent insists.' The commentary provides the proof from the hadith: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' The default oath is by Allah's name, specifically saying 'By Allah'. Swearing by other things like divorce or manumission is prohibited in the zahir al-riwaya. However, there is a difference of opinion among later scholars: some allow it in our time because people have lost reverence for oaths by Allah. The majority of mashayikh, however, do not permit it. If the judge does swear by divorce and the defendant refuses (nukul), the majority say the judgment is not executed. There is also a dispute about whether swearing by al-Rahman or al-Rahim counts as an oath. The author initially says it is not an oath, but al-Maqdisi refutes this, citing that all names of Allah are valid for oaths. The passage ends with a discussion of nukul and various opinions.

Key Terms
يمين (yamīn): An oath sworn in court, specifically by the name of Allah.
نكول (nukūl): Refusal to take an oath after it has been required; this can result in judgment against the refuser.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on a judge administering an oath by divorce?
A) Permissible if the opponent insists
B) Prohibited
C) Obligatory
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi court procedure, only an oath by Allah is valid; swearing by divorce is haram and produces no legal effect.

Ruling on Judicial Oaths: By Allah's Name Only
States the ruling on judicial oaths with proof and discusses an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on judicial oaths, identify the hadith evidence, and explain why oaths by divorce or manumission are prohibited and why the exceptional view is weak.

Core Idea
A judicial oath must be by Allah's name; swearing by divorce or manumission is prohibited.

Judicial oaths are a crucial part of court procedure. The Hanafi school, based on a clear prophetic directive, requires that the oath be taken only by the name of Allah. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and an intra-madhhab difference regarding exceptional circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act of administering an oath? What is the default ruling? The text states that the judge must swear the defendant by Allah's name, not by divorce or manumission.
The ruling is that divorce/manumission oaths are prohibited (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'Whoever swears among you, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' This is an ahad hadith, but its meaning is clear.
The dalil is from Tirmidhi and Ahmad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليحلف' indicates obligation to swear by Allah, and 'أو ليذر' prohibits swearing by anything else. Thus, the proof is established.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later scholars allowed divorce/manumission oaths if the plaintiff insists, due to people's disregard for Allah's name. But this view is outside Zahir al-Riwaya and is weak.
The majority, including the authoritative books, hold the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الدعوى القاضي واليمين بالله تعالى لا بطلاق وعتاق إلا إذا ألح الخصم ويغلظ بذكر أوصافه لا إلى آخر المجلس، فإن برهن في المجلس وإلا خلى سبيله، ولو قال أنا أخرج غداً أو إلى ثلاثة أيام يكفله إلى وقت الخروج وإن أنكر الطالب خروجه نظر إلى زيه أو بعث من يثق به إلى رفقائه، فإن قالوا أعد للخروج معنا يكفله إلى وقت الخروج اهـ. قوله : (واليمين بالله تعالى لا بطلاق وعتاق إلا إذا ألح الخصم) لقوله عليه السلام «من كان حالفاً منكم فيحلف بالله أو ليذر (۱) . وفي خزانة المفتين واليمين بالله تعالى ذكر اسمه تعالى وهو أن يقول والله ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لا تحليف بغير هذا الاسم، فلو حلفه بالرحمن أو لا يكون يميناً ولم أره صريحاً فلا يحلف بغيره من طلاق وعتاق، وقيل في زماننا إذا ألح الخصم ساغ للقاضي أن يحلف بذلك لقلة المبالاة باليمين بالله تعالى؛ كذا في الهداية. وظاهره أنه خارج عن ظاهر الرواية فما كان ينبغي للمؤلف ذكره في المتن لأنه موضوع لظاهر أنه ضعيف أيضاً لما في الخلاصة والتحليف بالطلاق والعتاق والأيمان المغلظة الرحيم الرواية مع هـ. لم يجوزه أكثر مشايخنا ا هـ . وفي الخانية : وإن أراد المدعي تحليفه بالطلاق والعتاق في ظاهر الرواية لا يجيبه القاضي إلى ذلك لأن التحليف بالطلاق والعتاق حرام، ومنهم من جوزه في زماننا والصحيح ما في ظاهر الرواية ا . وفي كتاب الحظر والإباحة من التتارخانية : والفتوى على عدم التحليف بالطلاق والعتاق ا هـ . وفي منية المفتي : لم يجزه أكثر مشايخنا وإن مست إليه الضرورة يفتى أن الرأي فيه للقاضي اتباعاً للبعض ا هـ . وفي خزانة المفتين كما في منية المفتي وزاد فلو حلفه القاضي بالطلاق فنكل وقضى بالمال لا ينفذ قضاؤه على قول الأكثر ا هـ. وظاهره أنه مفرع على قول الأكثر من أنه لا تحليف بهما فلا اعتبار بنكوله عنهما، وأما من قال بالتحليف بهما فيعتبر نكوله ويقضى به لأن التحليف بهما لرجاء النكول قوله : (فلو) حلفه بالرحمن أو الرحيم لا يكون يميناً ولم أره) رده العلامة المقدسي على ما نقل عنه الحموي بأنه قصور لوجود النص على خلافه فقد ذكروا في كتاب الأيمان أنه لو قال والرحمن أو الرحيم أو القادر فكل ذلك يمين ويدل عليه قولهم فيما إذا غلظ بذكر الصفة يحترز عن الإتيان بالواو لئلا تنكر اليمين، ونصوا هنا في تحليف الأخرس أن يقال له عهد الله عليك، ولا فرق بينه وبين الصحيح بل صرح بهذا في الصحيح، وصحح في روضة القضاة بأن الرحمن الرحيم وسائر أسماء الله تعالى تكون يميناً .اهـ. كذا في حاشية أبي السعود قوله : (نكوله) والظاهر من كلام الزيلعي خلافه حيث قال : وقال بعضهم يسوغ للقاضي أن يحلفه بهما إذا ألح الخصم لكن إذا نكل لا يقضى عليه بالنكول ولو قضى عليه بالنكول لا ينفذ اهـ. وفي غرر الأفكار مثله وعلله بقوله لامتناعه عما فليتأمل في هذا التعليل. وفي حاشية أبي السعود وفي الدر عن مصنف التنوير أنه هو منهي عنه (۱) رواه الترمذي في كتاب النذور باب . أحمد في مسنده (٢/ ٧).
Book of Claims: The judge (administers) the oath by Allah ta'ala, not by divorce or manumission, except when the opponent insists. And he intensifies by mentioning His attributes, not until the end of the session. Then if he presents proof in the session, (release him); otherwise, he is set free. If he says 'I will go out tomorrow or in three days', he guarantees him until the time of departure. If the plaintiff denies his departure, consideration is given to his appearance, or he sends a trustworthy person to his companions; if they say 'he is ready to depart with us', he guarantees him until departure. End of quote. His saying: (And the oath by Allah ta'ala, not by divorce or manumission, except when the opponent insists) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever swears among you, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' (1) In Khizanat al-Muftiyin: The oath by Allah ta'ala is by mentioning His name, which is to say 'wallah'. End. Its apparent meaning is that there is no administration of oath by other than this name. So if he swears him by al-Rahman, it is not an oath, and I have not seen it explicitly. So he should not swear by other than it from divorce and manumission. It was said in our time: if the opponent insists, it is permissible for the judge to swear him by that due to the lack of care for oaths by Allah ta'ala; thus in al-Hidaya. Its apparent meaning is that it is outside the well-known narration (zahir al-riwaya), so it was not befitting for the author to mention it in the text because it is based on what is apparent and it is weak as well, as in al-Khulasa: 'The administration of oath by divorce, manumission, and intensified oaths'—the majority of our mashayikh did not permit it. End. In al-Khaniyya: If the plaintiff wants to swear him by divorce or manumission, in the well-known narration the judge does not respond to him because swearing by divorce and manumission is haram. Some permitted it in our time, but the correct is what is in the well-known narration. End. In Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha from al-TatarKhaniyya: The fatwa is against swearing by divorce and manumission. End. In Munyat al-Mufti: The majority of our mashayikh did not permit it, and if necessity arises, a fatwa is given that the decision is for the judge, following some. End. In Khizanat al-Muftiyin, as in Munyat al-Mufti, and added: So if the judge swears him by divorce and he refuses and he judges with the property, his judgment is not executed according to the majority. End. Its apparent meaning is that it is based on the majority's view that there is no swearing by them, so his refusal is not considered. As for those who permit swearing by them, his refusal is considered and judgment is given, because swearing by them is for the hope of refusal. His saying: (So if) he swears him by al-Rahman or al-Rahim, it is not an oath and I have not seen it) was refuted by al-Maqdisi as transmitted by al-Hamawi, because it is a shortcoming due to the existence of a text to the contrary. They mentioned in the book of oaths that if he says 'by al-Rahman' or 'al-Rahim' or 'al-Qadir', all that is an oath. And their statement supports it: when he intensifies by mentioning the attribute, he avoids using the conjunction so that the oath is not denied. And they stated here regarding swearing the mute: it is said to him 'the covenant of Allah is upon you'. There is no difference between him and the sound person. Rather, they explicitly stated this in the sound person. And it was affirmed in Rawdat al-Qudah that al-Rahman, al-Rahim, and all the names of Allah ta'ala constitute an oath. End. Thus in Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud. His saying: (his refusal) and the apparent from al-Zayla'i's words is contrary, for he said: Some said it is permissible for the judge to swear him by them if the opponent insists, but if he refuses, he is not judged by refusal, and if he judges by refusal, it is not executed. End. In Ghurar al-Afkar, similar, and he reasoned it by saying: because he refrained from what he was prohibited from, so let it be considered. In Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud and al-Durr from the author of al-Tanwir, that it is prohibited. (1) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Vows, chapter. Ahmad in his Musnad (2/7).
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on judicial oaths in Hanafi law. The base ruling is that the oath must be by the name of Allah alone, specifically using the wording 'wallah'. The judge may not administer an oath by divorce or manumission, as that is prohibited (haram) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars. The evidence is a hadith: 'Whoever swears among you, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' The text then discusses an exception: if the plaintiff insists, some later scholars permit the judge to use divorce or manumission as the object of the oath, citing that people today are less fearful of swearing by Allah. However, this view is outside the well-known transmission (zahir al-riwaya) and is considered weak. The majority of Hanafi scholars (including those from the earlier authoritative books) do not permit it. The discussion then moves to whether swearing by 'al-Rahman' or 'al-Rahim' constitutes a valid oath. The initial statement that it does not is refuted by al-Maqdisi, who cites evidence from the books of oaths that all names of Allah are valid. The text also addresses the consequence of refusing to take such an oath: if the judge swears by divorce/emancipation and the defendant refuses, the judgment based on that refusal is not enforceable according to the majority, because the oath itself was improper. However, those who permit such oaths would consider the refusal and issue a judgment. The passage emphasizes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the prohibition of swearing by divorce and manumission.

Key Terms
التحليف بالطلاق والعتاق (al-tahlif bi al-talaq wa al-'itaq): Administering an oath using divorce or manumission as the subject of the oath (e.g., 'if I am lying, my wife is divorced').
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmission from the founding Imams, particularly from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after being asked by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (based on Zahir al-Riwaya), what is the ruling on administering a judicial oath by divorce or manumission?
A) It is obligatory to do so if the plaintiff insists
B) It is prohibited (haram) and the judge should not allow it
C) It is permissible but disliked
D) It is recommended to deter lying

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly requires judicial oaths to be by Allah's name only; any oath by divorce or manumission is prohibited and judgments based on such oaths are unenforceable.

Intensification of the Oath (Taghliz): By Attributes, Not by Time or Place
Defines taghliz method and prohibits time/place intensification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of intensifying a judicial oath in Hanafi fiqh and explain why intensification by time or place is not prescribed.

Core Idea
Intensify the oath by Allah's attributes, not by time or place – the purpose is veneration, not hardship.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how a judge may intensify an oath by mentioning Allah’s attributes, and clarifies that such intensification is not to be done by specifying a particular time or place. The underlying principle is to magnify the One sworn by, which is achieved without imposing additional hardship. The text also presents differing early Hanafi views on the permissibility of taghliz in general.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the definition of taghliz
Taghliz means adding descriptive attributes of Allah to an oath to increase its solemnity. It is not a pillar, but a discretionary enhancement.
2
Identify the permissible method
The judge may say: 'By Allah besides whom there is no god, Knower of the unseen and the seen, al-Rahman who knows the secret as He knows the public...' and may increase or decrease the wording as long as it does not cause multiple oaths.
3
Understand what is excluded
Taghliz by time (e.g., swearing at Friday prayer) or place (e.g., in the mosque) is not prescribed. The reason: veneration of Allah is already achieved without them, and requiring them causes hardship (haraj) for the judge or delays the plaintiff's right.
Al-Hidayah suggests permissibility but not obligation; al-Kafi and al-Muhit indicate it is not legislated.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The majority of early mashayikh did not permit taghliz at all. Later authorities (Khizanat al-Muftiyin) allow it at the judge's discretion. The mufta bihi permits attribute-based taghliz but rejects time/place intensification.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
If a judge requires a defendant to swear in a mosque, the defendant may refuse because such intensification is invalid. The essential oath is by Allah alone, and that has been fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويغلظ بذكر (أوصافه) مثل قوله والله الذي لا إله إلا هو عالم الغيب والشهادة الرحمن الذي يعلم من السر ما يعلم من العلانية ما لفلان هذا عليك ولا قبلك هذا المال الذي ادعاه وهو كذا وكذا ولا شيء منه، وله أن يزيد في التغليظ على هذا وينقص منه إلا أنه يحتاط كيلا تتكرر عليه اليمين لأن المستحق يمين واحدة وإن شاء القاضي لم يغلظ ويقتصر على بالله أو والله وقيل لا يغلظ على المعروف بالصلاح وقيل يغلظ في الخطير من المال دون الحقير، وقدمنا أن التغليظ لم يجوزه أكثر مشايخنا وذكر الشارح أنه لو حلف بالله ونكل عن التغليظ لا يقضى عليه بالنكول لأن المقصود الحلف بالله تعالى وقد حصل. وفي خزانة المفتين والاختيار في صفة التغليظ أن القضاة يزيدون فيه ما شاؤوا وينقصون ما شاؤوا ا هـ قوله : (لا) بزمان ومكان أي لا يغلظ القاضي بهما لأن المقصود تعظيم المقسم به وهو حاصل بدون ذلك وفي إيجاب ذلك حرج على القاضي حيث يكلف حضورها وهو مدفوع . وظاهر ما في الهداية أن المنفي وجوب التغليظ بهما فيدل على مشروعيته وإن لم يجب، وظاهر في الكتاب عدم المشروعية وظاهر قوله في الكافي لأن في التغليظ بالزمان تأخير حق المدعي في اليمين إلى ذلك الزمان أنه غير مشروع ولذا قال الشارح: فلا يشرع. وظاهر ما في المحيط أن التغليظ به ليس بحسن عندنا أصلاً فيفيد الإباحة ولكن ذكر بعده أنه لا يجوز ما التغليظ بالمكان .
His saying: (and he intensifies by mentioning [His] attributes) such as saying: 'by Allah besides whom there is no god, Knower of the unseen and the seen, al-Rahman who knows the secret as He knows the public, this amount is owed to so-and-so by you, and you do not have this money which he claims, and it is such-and-such, and you have nothing of it.' And he may increase or decrease in the intensification of this, except that he should be cautious so that the oath is not repeated on him, because what is due is one oath. If the judge wishes, he does not intensify and restricts to 'billah' or 'wallah'. It was said: he does not intensify for a person known for righteousness. It was said: he intensifies for significant wealth, not for insignificant. We have mentioned that the majority of our scholars did not permit intensification. And the commentator mentioned that if he swore by Allah and refused the intensification, he is not judged by refusal because the purpose is the oath by Allah ta'ala and it has been achieved. In Khizanat al-Muftiyin: the choice in the manner of intensification is that judges may increase as they wish and decrease as they wish. End. His saying: (not) by time and place, meaning the judge does not intensify by them because the purpose is to venerate the one sworn by, and that is achieved without that, and requiring that would cause hardship for the judge as he would be burdened with attendance, which is repelled. The apparent meaning of al-Hidayah is that the negation is of the obligation of intensification by them, which indicates its permissibility though not obligatory. The apparent meaning of the book is that it is not prescribed. The apparent meaning of al-Kafi is that intensification by time delays the plaintiff's right to the oath to that time, so it is not prescribed, hence the commentator said: it is not legislated. The apparent meaning of al-Muhit is that intensification by it is not good at all for us, which indicates permissibility, but later it mentions that intensification by place is not permissible.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the concept of taghliz (intensification) in judicial oaths. The judge may intensify the oath by mentioning attributes of Allah, such as His knowledge of the unseen and seen, etc. The judge has discretion to increase or decrease the wording, as long as it does not lead to multiple oaths. Some scholars hold that taghliz should not be applied to a known righteous person, and that it is only for significant amounts of property. Importantly, the passage clarifies that taghliz is not performed by specifying a time (e.g., swearing at a particular time) or a place (e.g., swearing in a specific location). The reason is that the purpose of intensification is to exalt the one sworn by (Allah), which is achieved without such temporal or spatial specifications. Moreover, requiring time or place would impose hardship on the judge. The text reviews different authorities: al-Hidayah suggests it is permissible but not obligatory; the book (presumably Kanz al-Daqa'iq) indicates it is not prescribed; al-Kafi states it is not prescribed because it delays the plaintiff's right; al-Muhit says it is not good at all, implying it is not allowed. The commentary also notes that if someone swears by Allah and refuses the intensification, he is not considered to have refused the oath (nukul) because the essential oath has been fulfilled.

Key Terms
التغليظ (al-taghliz): Intensifying the oath by adding descriptive attributes of Allah or other elements to increase its solemnity.
بزمان ومكان (bi zaman wa makan): Intensifying the oath by specifying a particular time (e.g., 'at the time of Friday prayer') or place (e.g., 'in the mosque').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on intensifying the oath by specifying a time (e.g., 'swear at the time of Friday prayer') according to the final position of the text?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is permissible but not recommended
C) It is not prescribed (la yushra')
D) It is a recommended part of taghliz

Key Takeaway
Intensification of the oath is performed by mentioning Allah's attributes, not by specifying a time or place, because the purpose is veneration without hardship.

Administering Oaths to Non-Muslims (Jew, Christian, Zoroastrian, Idolater)
Oath formulas for non-Muslim litigants in Hanafi judicial procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper Hanafi oath formulas for Jewish, Christian, Zoroastrian, and idolater litigants, and explain why pointing to a specific scripture copy is prohibited.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim's oath must be tailored to their sacred beliefs — the Jew by the Torah, Christian by the Gospel, Zoroastrian by fire, idolater by Allah alone.

In a Hanafi court, the oath (yamīn) is a serious matter, and its wording must carry weight for the litigant. Therefore, the school prescribes formulas that invoke what each religious community holds most sacred. This lesson presents the four formulas as recorded in the authoritative texts and the reasoning behind additional cautions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four non-Muslim categories
The passage explicitly distinguishes four categories: Jew (yahudi), Christian (nasrani), Zoroastrian (majusi), and idolater (wathani). Recognize that each is treated differently.
Idolaters include those who worship idols or multiple gods; the formula is simply 'by Allah'.
2
Memorize the oath formula for each
For each category, learn the precise wording: Jew: 'by Allah who sent down the Torah to Moses'; Christian: 'by Allah who sent down the Gospel to Jesus'; Zoroastrian: 'by Allah who created fire'; Idolater: 'by Allah' (without any specific reference).
The formulas are based on each religion's most sacred symbol or figure.
3
Understand the rationale for not pointing to a specific copy
The commentary from al-Bada'i' prohibits pointing to a particular physical copy of the Torah or Gospel when swearing, because these scriptures have been distorted; pointing might honor a corrupted text, which is impermissible.
This shows the Hanafi concern for tawqir (honoring) only authentic divine speech.
4
Analyze the discussion on swearing by divorce/emancipation
The text mentions that even if swearing by divorce/emancipation is not grounds for judgment, it serves to satisfy the plaintiff and deter lying, as the litigant fears personal consequences.
This is a secondary point showing the psychological dimension of oath-taking.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Given a litigant from a different religion (e.g., a Hindu), analogize to the nearest category (idolater) and use the general 'by Allah' formula, avoiding any specific reference that might be problematic.
The four categories may not cover all possibilities, but the principle is to use a formula meaningful to the litigant's faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويستحلف اليهودي بالله الذي أنزل التوراة على موسى عليه السلام والنصراني بالله الذي أنزل الانجيل على عيسى عليه السلام والمجوسي بالله الذي خلق النار والوثني بالله اعتمد ما في البحر لكن نقل السيد الحموي عن العلامة المقدسي ما محصله أن فائدة التحليف بهما على القول بأنه يجوز وإن كان لا يقضي عليه بالنكول اطمئنان خاطر المدعي إذا حلف فربما كان مشتبهاً عليه الأمر بنسيان ونحوه، فإذا حلف له بهما صدقه .اهـ. قلت بل في الغالب يمتنع عنه إذا كان كاذباً خوفاً من طلاق زوجته وعتق عبده فله فائدة تأمل قوله : ( إلا أنه يحتاط الخ) أي يحتاط عن العطف . قال الزيلعي : ولو أمر بالعطف فأتى بواحدة ونكل عن الباقي لا يقضى عليه بالنكول لأن المستحق عليه يمين واحدة وقد أتى بها قول المصنف : (ويستحلف اليهودي الخ) قال في البدائع : ولا يحلف على الإشارة إلى مصحف معين بأن يقول بالله الذي أنزل هذا التوراة أو هذا الإنجيل لأنه ثبت تحريف بعضها فلا يؤمن أن تقع الإشارة إلى الحرف المحرف فيكون التحليف به تعظيماً لما ليس كلام الله تعالى؛ كذا في الشرنبلالية .
His saying: (And the Jew is sworn by Allah who sent down the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, and the Christian by Allah who sent down the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, and the Zoroastrian by Allah who created fire, and the idolater by Allah.) He relied on what is in al-Bahr, but al-Sayyid al-Hamawi transmitted from al-Maqdisi that the gist is that the benefit of swearing by them (divorce/emancipation) on the view that it is permissible, even if he is not judged by refusal, is to satisfy the mind of the plaintiff, for perhaps he was confused due to forgetfulness and the like, so if he swears to him by them, he believes him. I say: rather, in most cases, he refrains from it if he is lying, fearing divorce of his wife and emancipation of his slave, so there is a benefit. Consider. His saying: (except that he is cautious, etc.) meaning cautious about the conjunction. Al-Zayla'i said: If he ordered the conjunction and he came with one and refused the rest, he is not judged by refusal because what is due on him is one oath and he has performed it. The author's saying: (And the Jew is sworn, etc.) He said in al-Bada'i': He should not swear by pointing to a specific copy (of the scriptures) by saying 'by Allah who sent down this Torah' or 'this Gospel' because it is established that some of them have been distorted, so it is not safe that the pointed part is distorted, and then the oath would be venerating what is not the word of Allah; thus in al-Sharnablaliyya.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage provides the method for administering oaths to non-Muslim litigants in a Hanafi court. Each non-Muslim community is sworn by Allah but with a reference that is meaningful to their faith: a Jew swears 'by Allah who sent down the Torah to Moses,' a Christian swears 'by Allah who sent down the Gospel to Jesus,' a Zoroastrian swears 'by Allah who created fire,' and an idolater swears simply 'by Allah.' The commentary then discusses a related point: the benefit of swearing by divorce and emancipation (even if not relied upon for judgment) is to reassure the plaintiff and deter lying. It also addresses caution against using a conjunctive 'and' in the oath to avoid multiplying oaths. Finally, it notes that one should not point to a specific physical copy of the Torah or Gospel when swearing, because those scriptures have been corrupted, and honoring a corrupted copy would be improper.

Key Terms
استحلاف (istihlaf): The act of administering an oath to a litigant by the judge.
اليهودي (al-yahudi): A Jewish person; in this context, a Jewish litigant who is to be sworn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is a Zoroastrian (Majusi) litigant sworn in a Hanafi court according to this passage?
A) By Allah who created fire
B) By Allah who sent down the Quran
C) By the sun and moon
D) By the Prophet Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge must use distinct, theologically appropriate oath formulas for non-Muslim litigants and must avoid pointing to corrupted scripture copies.

Ruling on Aggravating the Oath (Taqliz) with Attributes, Time, and Place
Commentary on the permissibility and specifics of aggravating the oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aggravation of a judicial oath (taghliz al-yamin) and apply the rule that refusal to use the aggravation formula does not constitute nukul (default).

Core Idea
Aggravating the oath is optional; swearing by Allah alone is sufficient and refusal to add more wording does not invalidate the oath or trigger default.

In judicial proceedings, an oath (yamin) is often administered to either party. The judge may choose to emphasize the oath by mentioning attributes of Allah or specifying a time or place - a practice called taghliz (aggravation). However, is this obligatory? What if the person refuses the extra wording? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position, resolving common misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'taghliz al-yamin' – aggravating the oath by mentioning attributes of Allah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory. The judge has discretion to increase or decrease the wording.
2
Note the intra-madhhab variation
Some early Hanafi scholars (mashayikhina) did not permit taqliz at all. Others permitted it. The later relied-upon position gives the judge full discretion as per Khizanat al-Muftin.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
3
Understand the effect of refusal to aggravate
If the defendant swears by Allah but refuses to add the aggravation wording, the oath is valid and no default (nukul) is incurred. The purpose is swearing by Allah, which has been fulfilled.
Nukul applies only if the essential oath is refused.
4
Examine the ruling on aggravation by time or place
The majority view is that aggravation by time (e.g., 'at the time of Friday prayer') or place (e.g., 'in the mosque') is not legislated. It causes hardship on the judge and delays the plaintiff's right.
Al-Hidayah suggests it is permissible but not obligatory; other authorities say it is not legislated at all.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling: judges may increase or decrease aggravation as they wish; aggravation by time or place is not practiced. The essential requirement is swearing by Allah.
This is from the later fatwa works and the commentator's choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويغلظ بذكر أوصافه مثل قوله والله الذي لا إله إلا هو عالم الغيب والشهادة الرحمن الذي يعلم من السر ما يعلم من العلانية ما لفلان هذا عليك ولا قبلك هذا المال الذي ادعاه وهو كذا وكذا ولا شيء منه، وله أن يزيد في التغليظ على هذا وينقص منه إلا أنه يحتاط كيلا تتكرر عليه اليمين لأن المستحق يمين واحدة وإن شاء القاضي لم يغلظ ويقتصر على بالله أو والله وقيل لا يغلظ على المعروف بالصلاح وقيل يغلظ في الخطير من المال دون الحقير، وقدمنا أن التغليظ لم يجوزه أكثر مشايخنا وذكر الشارح أنه لو حلف بالله ونكل عن التغليظ لا يقضى عليه بالنكول لأن المقصود الحلف بالله تعالى وقد حصل. وفي خزانة المفتين والاختيار في صفة التغليظ أن القضاة يزيدون فيه ما شاؤوا وينقصون ما شاؤوا ا هـ قوله : (لا) بزمان ومكان أي لا يغلظ القاضي بهما لأن المقصود تعظيم المقسم به وهو حاصل بدون ذلك وفي إيجاب ذلك حرج على القاضي حيث يكلف حضورها وهو مدفوع . وظاهر ما في الهداية أن المنفي وجوب التغليظ بهما فيدل على مشروعيته وإن لم يجب، وظاهر في الكتاب عدم المشروعية وظاهر قوله في الكافي لأن في التغليظ بالزمان تأخير حق المدعي في اليمين إلى ذلك الزمان أنه غير مشروع ولذا قال الشارح: فلا يشرع. وظاهر ما في المحيط أن التغليظ به ليس بحسن عندنا أصلاً فيفيد الإباحة ولكن ذكر بعده أنه لا يجوز التغليظ بالمكان .
His statement: (And he aggravates by mentioning His attributes) like saying: 'By Allah, there is no god but He, Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, the Most Merciful who knows the secret as He knows the open, that this person has no claim upon you, nor with you, this wealth which he claims, and it is such and such, and nothing of it.' And he may increase or decrease in the aggravation, except that he should be cautious so that the oath is not repeated upon him, because only one oath is due. If the judge wishes, he may not aggravate and restrict himself to 'By Allah' or 'By Allah'. It is said that he should not aggravate upon one known for righteousness, and it is said he aggravates in serious wealth, not trivial. And we have mentioned that most of our scholars did not permit aggravation, and the commentator mentioned that if he swears by Allah and refuses the aggravation, judgment is not passed against him for refusal (nukul) because the purpose is swearing by Allah, which has been fulfilled. In Khizanat al-Muftin: 'The choice in the description of aggravation is that judges may increase or decrease in it as they wish.' His statement: (Not) with time or place means that the judge should not aggravate by them, because the purpose is to honor the one sworn by, which is achieved without that, and requiring that would cause hardship on the judge since he is burdened with attending them, and that is repelled. The apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that the negation refers to the obligation of aggravation by them, which indicates its permissibility even if not obligatory. The apparent meaning in the book (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) is that it is not legislated, and the apparent meaning of his statement in al-Kafi is: 'Because aggravation by time delays the plaintiff's right to the oath until that time, it is not legislated.' Hence the commentator said: 'So it is not legislated.' The apparent meaning in al-Muhit is that aggravation by them is not good at all according to us, which indicates permissibility, but he mentioned after that that it is not permissible to aggravate by place.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on aggravating an oath (taqliz) in court proceedings. The author first describes the recommended wording for aggravation, which includes mentioning multiple attributes of Allah to emphasize the oath's solemnity. However, the judge has discretion: he may use this or a simpler formula like 'By Allah'. There is disagreement among Hanafi scholars: some say aggravation is not permissible, especially for a person known for piety; others say it depends on the amount of wealth involved. Importantly, the commentator clarifies that if the defendant swears by Allah but refuses the additional wording, he is not held in default (nukul) because the essential purpose of swearing by Allah is achieved. The passage then tackles the question of aggravating by specifying a time or a place (e.g., swearing 'by Allah, at the time of Friday prayer' or 'in the mosque'). The author explains that this is not done because it places unnecessary hardship on the judge (who would have to attend) and delays the plaintiff's right. The great Hanafi authorities like al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, and al-Muhit are cited: the prevailing view is that aggravation by time or place is not legislated or at least not good practice, though it may be considered permissible (mubah) but not recommended. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that judges have full discretion to choose the level of aggravation, increasing or decreasing as they see fit, as stated in Khizanat al-Muftin. This ruling guards against the misunderstanding that aggravation is obligatory or that its omission invalidates the oath.

Key Terms
تغليظ اليمين (taghliz al-yamin): Aggravating the oath by swearing with additional attributes of Allah or specifying time/place to emphasize its solemnity.
نكول (nukul): Refusal to take an oath after it has been demanded; results in judgment against the refuser.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person swears by Allah but refuses to use the additional formula of taqliz (aggravation)?
A) The oath is invalid and the person is held in default.
B) The oath is valid and no default is incurred.
C) The judge must force him to use the additional formula.
D) The oath is valid but the person must repeat it with taqliz.

Key Takeaway
Aggravating a judicial oath with attributes is permissible but not obligatory; refusal to aggravate does not constitute default, and aggravation by time or place is not practiced in the Hanafi school.

Administering Oaths to Non-Muslims: Formulas and Disputes
Determining the correct oath formula for non-Muslims and resolving disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and al-Khassaf on the oath formula for non-Muslims, and apply the mufta bihi ruling that the formula is taqliz (aggravation), not a condition.

Core Idea
Swearing by Allah alone suffices for all; specific formulas are taqliz, not conditions.

In Hanafi courts, administering oaths to non-Muslim witnesses requires consideration of their beliefs. The standard position in Kanz al-Daqa'iq prescribes specific formulas for Jews, Christians, Magians, and idolaters. However, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute questions whether these formulas are obligatory or merely recommended. This lesson examines the evidence, the contrasting views of Abu Hanifa, al-Khassaf, and Imam Muhammad, and the operative ruling that the essential element is swearing by Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories and Formulas
From the source, list each non-Muslim group and the specific formula mentioned for their oath.
Jew: 'by Allah who revealed the Torah'; Christian: 'by Allah who revealed the Gospel'; Magian: 'by Allah who created the fire'; Idolater: 'by Allah'.
2
Trace the Evidence
The hadith of Ibn Suriya is cited as evidence for the formula. Understand how it supports the practice.
The Prophet used a formula mentioning the Torah when questioning a Jewish scholar.
3
Compare the Intra-Hanafi Positions
Identify the views of Abu Hanifa (swear all by Allah alone), al-Khassaf (special formulas only for Jews and Christians), and Imam Muhammad (formulas as in the book). Note the reasoning behind each.
Abu Hanifa: no specific formula needed; Khassaf: only revealed books merit mention; Muhammad: custom and analogical extension to Magians.
4
Analyze the Practical Question
The text asks: if a non-Muslim swears only by Allah and refuses the special formula, is it sufficient? Determine the conclusion.
The author concludes the extra wording is taqliz, not a condition; swearing by Allah alone suffices.
5
Synthesize the Mufta Bihi
Combine the positions to state the operative ruling for fatwa: the formulas are recommended but not obligatory; the essential is swearing by Allah.
Al-Muhit indicates that the book's view is Imam Muhammad's, and Khassaf's is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The mufta bihi accepts the formulas but treats them as taqliz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويستحلف اليهودي بالله الذي أنزل التوراة على موسى عليه السلام والنصراني بالله الذي أنزل الانجيل على عيسى عليه السلام والمجوسي بالله الذي خلق النار والوثني بالله لقوله عليه السلام لابن صوريا الأعور أنشدك بالله الذي أنزل التوراة على موسى أن حكم الزنا في كتابكم هذا، ولأن اليهودي يعتقد نبوة موسى عليه السلام، والنصراني نبوة عيسى فيغلظ على كل واحد بذكر المنزل على نبيه وما ذكره من صورة تحليف المجوسي مذكور في الأصل، ويروى عن الإمام الأعظم أنه لا يستحلف أحد إلا بالله تعالى خالصاً. وذكر الخصاف أنه لا يستحلف غير اليهودي والنصراني إلا بالله وهو اختيار بعض المشايخ لأن ذكر النار اسمه تعالى تعظيم لها وما ينبغي أن تعظم بخلاف الكتابين لأن كتب الله تعالى معظمة والوثني لا يحلف إلا بالله تعالى لأن الكفرة بأسرهم يعتقدون الله تعالى قال الله تعالى ولئن سألتهم من خلق السموات والأرض ليقولن الله [لقمان: ٢٥] وظاهر ما في المحيط أن ما في الكتاب قول محمد، وما ذكره الخصاف قولهما فإن قلت : إذا حلف الكافر بالله فقط ونكل عما ذكر هل يكفيه أم لا؟ قلت: لم أره صريحاً وظاهر قولهم أنه يغلظ به أنه ليس بشرط وأنه من باب التغليظ فيكتفي بالله ولا يقضى عليه بالنكول عن الوصف المذكور وفي العناية : ابن صوريا بالقصر اسم أعجمي وأنشدك أي أحلفك بالله ا هـ. وذكر ابن الكمال أن الكفرة بأسرهم لا يعتقدون الله تعالى فإن الدهرية منهم لا يعتقدونه ولا دلالة في قوله تعالى ولئن سألتهم الآية. على ذلك بل لأن الوثني يعبد غير الله تعالى ويعتقد أن الله تعالى واليهودي نسبة إلى هود وهو اسم نبي عربي وسمي بالجمع وبالمضارع من هاد إذا ، ويقال هم يهود وهو غير منصرف للعلمية ووزن الفعل وجاز تنوينه، وقيل نسبة إلى يهود بن يعقوب عليهما السلام وتمامه في المصباح وفيه رجل نصراني بفتح النون وامرأة نصرانية وربما قيل نصران ونصرانة ويقال هو نسبة إلى قرية اسمها نصرة؟ قاله الواحدي . ولهذا قيل في الواحد نصري على القياس والنصارى جمعه مثل مهري ومهارى، ثم أطلق النصراني على كل من تعبد بهذا الدين ا هـ . وفيه : المجوس أمة من الناس وهي وتمجس دخل في دين المجوس كما يقال تهود أو تنصر إذا دخل في دين اليهود والنصارى وفيه : الوثن الصنم سواء كان من خشب أو حجر أو غيره، والجمع وثن مثل أسد وأسد وأوثان وينسب إليه من يتدين بعبادته على لفظه فيقال رجل وثني ا هـ قوله: (ولا يحلفون في بيوت عبادتهم لأن القاضي لا يحضرها بل هو ممنوع عن ذلك؛ كذا في الهداية . ولو قال المسلم لا يحضرها لكان أولى لما في التتارخانية : يكره للمسلم الدخول في البيعة والكنيسة، وإنما يكره من حيث إنه مجمع الشياطين لا من حيث إنه ليس له حق الدخول، والظاهر أنها تحريمية لأنها المرادة عند إطلاقها وقد أفتيت بتعزير مسلم لازم الكنيسة مع خالقه ا هـ.
His statement: (And the Jew is sworn by Allah who revealed the Torah to Moses, peace be upon him, and the Christian by Allah who revealed the Gospel to Jesus, peace be upon him, and the Magian by Allah who created the fire, and the idolater by Allah) because of his statement, peace be upon him, to Ibn Suriya the one-eyed: 'I adjure you by Allah who revealed the Torah to Moses: what is the ruling of adultery in your book?' And because the Jew believes in the prophethood of Moses, and the Christian in the prophethood of Jesus, so each is aggravated by mentioning what was revealed to his prophet. What he mentioned of the formula for swearing the Magian is mentioned in al-Asl. And it is narrated from Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) that he did not swear anyone except by Allah alone. And Khassaf mentioned that he does not swear other than the Jew and the Christian except by Allah, and this is the choice of some of the scholars, because mentioning the fire is the name of a creation, glorifying it, and it should not be glorified, unlike the two books because the books of Allah are glorified. And the idolater is sworn only by Allah, because all the disbelievers believe in Allah. Allah said: 'And if you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say: Allah' [Luqman 25]. The apparent meaning in al-Muhit is that what is in the book (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) is the saying of Muhammad, and what Khassaf mentioned is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). So if you say: If the disbeliever swears by Allah only and refuses what was mentioned, is it sufficient for him or not? I say: I have not seen it explicitly, but the apparent meaning of their saying 'he aggravates with it' is that it is not a condition, and it is from the chapter of aggravation, so he is satisfied with Allah and not judged for refusal regarding the mentioned description. And in al-Inayah: 'Ibn Suriya' with shortening is a foreign name, and 'anshadaka' means I make you swear by Allah. And Ibn al-Kamal mentioned that all the disbelievers do not believe in Allah, for the Dahriyya among them do not believe in Him, and there is no indication in the verse 'And if you ask them' of that, rather because the idolater worships other than Allah and believes that Allah... And 'Yahudi' is a relative adjective to Hud, who is an Arab prophet, and it is derived from the plural and the imperfect of 'hada' if... and it is said they are Jews, and it is indeclinable for properness and verb form, and its tanwin is permissible. And it is said it is relative to Yahudh ibn Ya'qub. And its completion is in al-Misbah. And therein: a man 'nasrani' with fatha on the nun, and a woman 'nasraniyya', and occasionally it is said 'nasran' and 'nasrana'. And it is said it is relative to a village called Nasra? Said by al-Wahidi. Hence it is said for the singular 'nasri' on analogy, and 'nasara' is its plural like 'muhri' and 'mahari'. Then 'nasrani' is used for everyone who follows this religion. And therein: 'Majus' is a nation of people, and 'tamajjasa' means to enter the religion of the Majus, just as one says 'tahawwada' or 'tanassara' if they enter Judaism or Christianity. And therein: 'Wathan' is an idol, whether of wood, stone, or other. The plural is 'wathn' like 'asad' and 'usud' and 'awthan'. One who worships it is called 'wathani'. His statement: (And they are not sworn in their places of worship) because the judge does not attend them; rather he is prohibited from that; as in al-Hidayah. And if a Muslim said he does not attend, it would be more appropriate; as in al-Tatarkhaniyya: It is makruh for a Muslim to enter a synagogue or church, and it is only makruh because it is a gathering of devils, not because he has no right to enter. And the apparent ruling is that it is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it is what is intended when it is said. And I have given a fatwa of ta'zir (discretionary punishment) for a Muslim who frequents a church with its creator.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage details the formulas for administering oaths to non-Muslims in a Hanafi court. The standard position (stated in Kanz al-Daqa'iq and attributed to Imam Muhammad) is: a Jew is sworn 'by Allah who revealed the Torah to Moses', a Christian 'by Allah who revealed the Gospel to Jesus', a Magian 'by Allah who created the fire', and an idolater simply 'by Allah'. The proof is the Prophet's (saw) practice with the Jewish scholar Ibn Suriya. However, there is a notable intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly held that no one should be sworn except by Allah alone, regardless of religion. Al-Khassaf limited the special formulas only to Jews and Christians, while all others (Magians, idolaters) are sworn only by Allah. This is because mentioning the fire glorifies a creation, which is not appropriate, whereas the Torah and Gospel are revered as revealed books. The passage then addresses a practical question: if a non-Muslim swears by Allah but refuses the additional formula (e.g., 'who revealed the Torah'), is it sufficient? The author concludes it is sufficient and the person is not held in default, because the additional formula is mere aggravation (taqliz), not a condition. The discussion also includes a refutation of Ibn al-Kamal's claim that disbelievers do not believe in Allah, citing the Quranic verse that even polytheists acknowledge Allah as Creator. The lesson ends with the ruling that non-Muslims are not sworn in their places of worship because the judge should not enter them, and it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for Muslims to enter churches or synagogues.

Key Terms
تغليظ (taghliz): The act of making an oath more solemn by adding specific words, in this context for non-Muslims.
مجوسي (majusi): A follower of Zoroastrianism (Magian), called 'majusi' from 'majus'.
وثني (wathani): An idolater who worships idols (wathan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) in this text, what happens if a Jew is asked to swear 'by Allah who revealed the Torah to Moses' but he only swears 'by Allah'?
A) The oath is invalid and the Jew is held in default.
B) The oath is valid and he is not held in default.
C) The judge must force him to say the full formula.
D) The Jew must be re-sworn in a synagogue.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, oaths to non-Muslims use specific formulas as aggravation, but swearing by Allah alone is always sufficient.
